<div id="review_1250814490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1250814490" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1250814490?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1250814490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11134414009236473865">That goblin was just the sweetest child emperor I've ever known. He was always courteous and polite, even when he was abducted. He was so centered and contained even during that that time he almost took the knife of that assassin. Do you remember his name? Yeah. That windbag elf. Well, I don't care what any of his peers say about this dear child. He's looking forward to the future, I tell you! He even says goodbye to the cleaning staff of his late mother, bless his soul.<br/><br/>This novel, in case you h</span>
  <span id="freeText11134414009236473865" style="display:none">That goblin was just the sweetest child emperor I've ever known. He was always courteous and polite, even when he was abducted. He was so centered and contained even during that that time he almost took the knife of that assassin. Do you remember his name? Yeah. That windbag elf. Well, I don't care what any of his peers say about this dear child. He's looking forward to the future, I tell you! He even says goodbye to the cleaning staff of his late mother, bless his soul.<br /><br />This novel, in case you haven't guessed, is a delightful take on normal people raising an Emperor. It is NOT, however, a tale of war, oppression, or magic. There's plenty of intrigue, but mainly it's a coming of age with a very healthy dose of fish out of water syndrome. On a personal note, it was charming and well paced and very, very political. It had elements of stab you in the back, of course, but the focus was mainly on trying to do a good job in a situation where no one seems to trust you. Believe me, I was very charmed.<br /><br />This delightful novel was part of this year's Hugo nominations, and in spite of the controversy, I'm reading each novel deeply and seriously because I respect and cherish the Hugos. Anyone nominated will carry prestige because we, the readers, want it to be so. The moment we start devaluing the award in our own minds is the moment we lose a little light in our life.<br /><br />As for being a contender, this novel definitely is. If I read this outside of the controversy or the nomination, I would still be gibbering and drooling about it, because, after all, it turns our archetypal conventions over to cook more evenly.<br /><br />The writing is clear, the story is suspenseful, and the mystery around his father's death and his own assassination attempt keeps everything moving nicely. Most importantly, I felt real sympathy for our dear Emperor. If you think that the story is short on wonder or depth, think again. Everything is vividly imagined and deeply drawn, down to the airships or the clockwork bridge or the guard who sang our young Emperor to sleep.<br /><br />This novel is a breath of fresh air with a huge heart, and that's saying a lot for a novel about a goblin.<br /><br /><a href="http://danrymes.blogspot.ca/" rel="nofollow noopener">Brad K Horner's blog</a></span>

<div id="review_900529345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900529345" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900529345?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900529345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11707966514991996636">This was an enjoyable read. The story was engaging despite not being all that exciting. This was a character driven fantasy that mainly focused on court intrigue. <br/><br/>Maia, who is half goblin, has spent his entire life living in an isolated country estate. First being looked after by his mother and then his banished cousin after his mother died. As the outcast fourth son he was largely ignored and forgotten by the court and his cruel neglectful father. An accident on an airship changes all this as t</span>
  <span id="freeText11707966514991996636" style="display:none">This was an enjoyable read. The story was engaging despite not being all that exciting. This was a character driven fantasy that mainly focused on court intrigue. <br /><br />Maia, who is half goblin, has spent his entire life living in an isolated country estate. First being looked after by his mother and then his banished cousin after his mother died. As the outcast fourth son he was largely ignored and forgotten by the court and his cruel neglectful father. An accident on an airship changes all this as the Emperor and his three eldest sons are killed. Maia is recalled to court to take his place as Emperor. <br /><br />This story chronicled his rise from a naive boy who was intimidated by his lack of social skills and education into a fairly benevolent ruler. I liked the way Maia slowly developed as a character. He was a genuinely good guy, but felt like a realistic enough character. He was lonely and intimidated in the early stages buy grew more confident in his own decisions as he gained more knowledge and experience. He was no superman. He needed time and help to solve his problems.<br /><br />The Elvish court was not always welcoming to Maia and he had to fight off a few plots to overthrow him as emperor. I enjoyed this aspect of the story. The motivations of those plotting against him were well explained and easily understood. <br /><br />This book was not without faults. The pacing was a bit slow and the Elvish and Goblin names were a nightmare. They were too similar. I also felt like the racial tensions between the Goblins and Elves was more hinted at than fully explored. <br /><br />Despite being set in a fantasy world and being a story about Goblins and Elves this could have been a coming of age tale for any young royal in a historical setting. The characters were very human in their emotions and actions and while magic was hinted at it played almost no part in the story.<br /><br />Rating: 4 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: This was narrated by Kyle McCarley. I thought he was a perfect fit for the formal language of the story. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11707966514991996636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Geoff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5999881-geoff"><img alt="Geoff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312918140p2/5999881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1096864850?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geoff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geoff" href="/user/show/5999881-geoff">Geoff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5999881-geoff?shelf=locus-winner">locus-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5999881-geoff?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5999881-geoff?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096864850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14279992680439033897">Despite the generally great ratings & reviews of this book, and its recent Nebula nomination, this book did not bring ‘it’ in many categories.<br/><br/>The good: Maia, the new emperor, is a great character. Despite his lack of confidence, he performs admirably in his new job with the help of his secretary, Csevet.<br/><br/>The not-so-good: The world. I’ve seen in some places this book be called a ‘fantasy of manners’. I suppose there are readers who would be interested in this kind of thing but it’s definitely not </span>
  <span id="freeText14279992680439033897" style="display:none">Despite the generally great ratings &amp; reviews of this book, and its recent Nebula nomination, this book did not bring ‘it’ in many categories.<br /><br />The good: Maia, the new emperor, is a great character. Despite his lack of confidence, he performs admirably in his new job with the help of his secretary, Csevet.<br /><br />The not-so-good: The world. I’ve seen in some places this book be called a ‘fantasy of manners’. I suppose there are readers who would be interested in this kind of thing but it’s definitely not for me. There are blocks of text devoted to dressing the emperor, or the correct way to reply to a letter, or the various divisions in the government. In some books this is presented in an interesting way, but here, the reader has to read dry text that describes what is going on. Also in this category (I think) is the very specific naming conventions used in the social hierarchy which can be quite daunting at times. And could it have hurt anyone to put a map in the book. I’m sure it’s more work than I realize but it would be appreciated. (There is a map on the author’s website but its hand-drawn and hard to read in areas)<br /><br />The bad: The plot. I don’t like going deep into plot in my reviews but the lack of planning with the conspiracies in this novel needs to be addressed. It was sloppy work all around. Even the nefarious plots that do work suffer from poor execution. They are an amazing example of ineptitude. There are various subplots (marriages, funerals, etc) but they all turn out pretty good. They probably had better planners than the conspirators.<br /><br />Its not a bad book but it wasn’t for me. I feel as if my opinions will not parallel those of the Sword &amp; Laser book club, and anxiously await their opinions.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14279992680439033897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_898057732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/898057732" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/898057732?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer898057732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12087218367713064234">This is a charming tale of an unprepared young man, launched into a world that would be daunting even if he had been trained for it. Exiled by his father, abused by his guardian, disregarded and despised by everyone but his mother, Maia must find his way in a court that is complicated, unforgiving, and hostile.<br/><br/>I appreciated some of the real world concerns that found their way into this work of fantasy: the issue of skin colour, the status of women, the ways that people treat one another as “less</span>
  <span id="freeText12087218367713064234" style="display:none">This is a charming tale of an unprepared young man, launched into a world that would be daunting even if he had been trained for it. Exiled by his father, abused by his guardian, disregarded and despised by everyone but his mother, Maia must find his way in a court that is complicated, unforgiving, and hostile.<br /><br />I appreciated some of the real world concerns that found their way into this work of fantasy: the issue of skin colour, the status of women, the ways that people treat one another as “lesser than.” I also enjoyed the steampunk details included in the book.<br /><br />Although there is violence—it begins with the airship explosion that kills the Emperor and the three sons ahead of Maia for the throne after all—this is not a novel about war, battle or force. This is a tale about kindness conquering all and about how much it matters who the man or woman at the top of the hierarchy is. Years ago, I was involved in a large organization as a volunteer when said organization hired a man of dubious reputation as CEO. Rumour had it that he had quit the last executive position before sexual harassment charges could catch up with him. Soon, all the women in our organization were on high alert and knew to never be alone with this creep. Eventually even the men on staff figured things out and finally Mr. Creepy CEO was turfed, but the organization continues to suffer from the years he spent at the helm. One of my male friends told me that he had always considered that it really didn’t matter who was at the top of the heap, that he just ignored that detail and did his job—until this situation, when he realized that company culture really does emanate downwards from the person in charge.<br /><br />Having said all of that, Maia demonstrates that the Golden Rule is an excellent way to run one’s life or one’s kingdom—do unto others as you would have them do unto you. He doesn’t win every encounter by practicing this philosophy, but by unflinchingly attempting to be fair, to really listen to people and to care, he shows the qualities of a real leader.<br /><br />Two criticisms, both to do with names: one, Maia to me sounds like a female name and it bugged me attached to a male character. Two, there were too many very complicated names. If the names had dissimilar or if there had been fewer characters, I might have had a hope of keeping them straight. As it was, when one turned out to be important, I had to backtrack a bit and figure out exactly who they were. Otherwise, I just treated them as background wallpaper and didn’t try to distinguish one from another—and this despite the fact that I am usually good with names and that fictional names actually matter a great deal to me.<br /><br />Despite the naming issues, I enjoyed this book very much and in fact stayed up much too late one evening to finish it. I am still trying to catch up on sleep, but The Goblin Emperor was worth it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12087218367713064234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1204166789" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204166789" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204166789?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=sword-and-laser">sword-and-laser</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204166789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17360031783042709821"><b>Executive Summary:</b> The second half of this book is far superior to the first half making for a rather enjoyable read for me in the end. It won't be for everyone though.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I must say I'm surprised to be giving this such a high rating. And not a 3.5 rounded up, but a solid 4. At the start of the book this was more like the 2.5 area.<br/><br/>The writing is fine. The world building, though sparse was decent. And I liked Maia from the start. With the reading funk I was in, this seemed like a good </span>
  <span id="freeText17360031783042709821" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> The second half of this book is far superior to the first half making for a rather enjoyable read for me in the end. It won't be for everyone though.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I must say I'm surprised to be giving this such a high rating. And not a 3.5 rounded up, but a solid 4. At the start of the book this was more like the 2.5 area.<br /><br />The writing is fine. The world building, though sparse was decent. And I liked Maia from the start. With the reading funk I was in, this seemed like a good option to get me out of it. But despite all that I was bored. I barely touched it for a week. I'd read maybe one chapter a night. I skipped a few nights without reading it all. There just didn't seem to be much plot. Maia kept meeting a bunch of people whose names I still can't keep straight.<br /><br />Then somewhere around the midway point, the plot finally seemed to kick in and I was hooked. I read the first 200 pages in 12 days. I read the rest of the book in 2. I was hoping to put a good dent in this book this weekend because it's due back to the library soon. I wasn't expecting to finish it.<br /><br />If it hadn't been a group pick, I might have quit on it. I haven't quit on a book in years though, and I didn't hate it, I just wasn't really into it either. <br /><br />I'm really glad I stuck with it. It was a lot of fun. I just wish the first half of it hadn't been so slow. I think that may turn a lot of people off who might end up liking it in the end as I did. There are just too many books out there to stick it out.<br /><br />I'm not sure if this deserves the Nebula it's been nominated for, but I can see why it was nominated. But I expect a lot of people will question it however. The sense of danger prevalent in most fantasy novels is never really there. The conflicts may be a bit too light/easy for some. For me though, it was just what I needed.<br /><br />And I'm glad that it's a stand alone. That is so rare these days. I'd read more books about Maia, but I think sort of coming of age/learning how to rule story is sufficient as it is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17360031783042709821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1098126142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098126142" />
    <a title="Alissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24456819-alissa"><img alt="Alissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426345849p2/24456819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1098126142?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alissa" href="/user/show/24456819-alissa">Alissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17404280-the-goblin-emperor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24456819-alissa?shelf=read-ebooks">read-ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1098126142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11371435832707871241">5 heartfelt stars. This novel is one of those rare gems that are probably even more valuable over time and it’s all wrapped up in a neat, standalone package.<br/><br/>The beginning is very powerful: at I first struggled a bit to fall into step because everything is not laid out cut and dried before the reader and there are lots of nuances to catch and names to remember, but soon I was utterly and helplessly drawn into Maia's reality. <br/>It’s a testament to the author’s skill that she achieved such delicate b</span>
  <span id="freeText11371435832707871241" style="display:none">5 heartfelt stars. This novel is one of those rare gems that are probably even more valuable over time and it’s all wrapped up in a neat, standalone package.<br /><br />The beginning is very powerful: at I first struggled a bit to fall into step because everything is not laid out cut and dried before the reader and there are lots of nuances to catch and names to remember, but soon I was utterly and helplessly drawn into Maia's reality. <br />It’s a testament to the author’s skill that she achieved such delicate balance of worldbuilding and pacing when political scheming is the main entry on the menu.<br /><br />Maia himself is a big part of the experience because he’s a believable protagonist: not rash, nor unrealistically naïve or flawless. He is the son of an unwanted bride and was never raised at court but he is suddenly cast in the role of Emperor of the Eflands; all too aware of his own ignorance but by no means aggressive or gullible, he tries to adjust -between success and failure- and this was refreshing. Consequently, his logic dovetailed nicely with mine and the connection was instantaneous.<br /><br />The (many!) secondary characters are no less important or developed, ranging from vacuous young men who had always enjoyed a smooth life to manipulative statespeople to grieving courtiers, they all play a part in this elaborate game of etiquette and power, and as such, expect more subtlety than action.<br /><br />And finally there is the court itself, <i>"the drunken hornet’s nest that is the Untheileneise Court”</i>, a paragon of virtue and vice and a memorable character on its own right.<br /><br />If you like intricate machinations, unpredictability, beautiful descriptions and remarkable protagonists (a good memory won’t come amiss, too), you’re probably going to have a great time with this fantasy of manners.<br /><br /><br /><i>he began to feel that he had alliances, that his life—for perhaps the first time since his mother died—was not merely a matter of surviving from one hostile encounter to the next.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11371435832707871241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1140025108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1140025108" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18378839-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363322629p2/18378839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1140025108?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/18378839-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1140025108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1310540913085101848">41. THE GOBLIN EMPEROR, BY KATHERINE ADDISON<br/><br/>Recommended to me by Leonardo, on Goodreads, and some "best fantasy books” lists. As I understand it, he hasn’t actually read it, but plans to. Honestly, I wouldn’t bother.<br/><br/>Synopsis: A half goblin, half elf boy, son of the elven emperor, is astonished to discover that, since his father and all his brothers have died in an accident, he’s the heir to the throne. He goes to the palace where he meets lots of people and watches some things happening.<br/><br/>Overall </span>
  <span id="freeText1310540913085101848" style="display:none">41. THE GOBLIN EMPEROR, BY KATHERINE ADDISON<br /><br />Recommended to me by Leonardo, on Goodreads, and some "best fantasy books” lists. As I understand it, he hasn’t actually read it, but plans to. Honestly, I wouldn’t bother.<br /><br />Synopsis: A half goblin, half elf boy, son of the elven emperor, is astonished to discover that, since his father and all his brothers have died in an accident, he’s the heir to the throne. He goes to the palace where he meets lots of people and watches some things happening.<br /><br />Overall enjoyment: I tried very hard, but just couldn’t like it. Every time I try to come up with a redeeming quality, I almost immediately shoot it down. It was just boring and badly written.<br /><br />Plot: There isn’t one. It’s a bunch of stuff that happens, one after the other, and almost unconnected. And even those small plots are boring, ridiculously incongruent, obvious, and badly made.<br /><br />Characters: Again, bleh. The only character with some depth is Maia himself; all the others are two- or one-dimensional profoundly stupid beings. You can tell right away who is good and who is bad depending on if they are warmly welcoming to him or if they look at him with pure hatred. His enemies are so stupid it’s a wonder they manage to get anything done; you can see right through every one of their plots, and I believe my grandmother could have come up with better plans for assassinating the emperor. And she has Alzheimer’s. The good characters are good just because they are. And despite being marginally better written, Maia is also a very badly developed character. He’s very inconsistent, being a political genius and infinitely wise in one chapter and naive boy who probably still believes in Santa and would sign contracts against the presents he would bring. He’s so pusillanimous; nothing in the story happens because of him, he only watches while things happen.<br /><br />World/setting: I was hoping this could be a redeeming quality, but, sadly, it’s not. It’s simply a badly constructed world. She did put some work into it, but all in the wrong places. You have no idea how the society works, she completely ignores the day to day life of people, but she gives excruciatingly detailed descriptions of formalities and rituals among the nobles. And they’re not even useful formalities, they are not metaphors of how the society works, or significant to the plot, characters or ideas; they’re just whimsical empty gestures designed to give the impression of a culture. She invents terms and titles and just dumps them on the reader’s lap without any explanation. Plus, her choices of what to describe really leave something to be desired; she keeps building up expectations, saying how wonderful, amazing, extraordinary and impressive things are and then, when the character finally sees this thing, they will assure the reader that it really is and not describe it at all (in the meantime, the reader will know every meal and every piece of clothing in the area around in detail). This world was supposed to have steampunk elements, and indeed there is mention of a few steam-powered engines and such, but it has absolutely nothing to do with the story and could have been removed without loss (the book probably would have been better, because it would be shorter). It feels like she only included them as an afterthought, so her book would be considered steampunk.<br /><br />Writing style: I don’t it. Very obscure, almost like she’s purposefully trying to make her text more difficult to read. The pronouns seem like an unnecessary affectation (much like almost everything in this book). She will travel wildly in time and space in the same chapter (sometimes even the same paragraph), without any warning.<br /><br />Representation: There was an attempt, with the goblins being dark skinned and suffering some prejudice from it and a few homosexual relationships, it’s very badly worked (or not at all). Just like with the steampunk, it feels like she only included them so that it would be there.<br /><br />Political correctness: This book is a goddamn train wreck. All the characters are stereotypes. She’s very bad on her treatment of women: there are very few, and those are very stupid or absolutely motherly. But then, the male characters are very badly written too, so that’s probably not sexism.<br /><br />Up next: The Glass Castle, by Jeannette Walls<br /><a href="https://1drv.ms/u/s!AvjP4beB9w9clIsCRuRtdW0dhgSMjA" rel="nofollow noopener">JL 740</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1310540913085101848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_809009675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/809009675" />
    <a title="Sherwood Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith"><img alt="Sherwood Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543007644p2/162084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/809009675?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sherwood Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sherwood Smith" href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith">Sherwood Smith</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17404280-the-goblin-emperor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162084-sherwood-smith?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer809009675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3588063412517282304">I read this novel in draft a year ago. I just checked to see when it would be published--April. So I will have more to say when I get the actual book.<br/><br/>But it is on my buy-at-once list: since it's not out there is little to say that isn't spoilery. but put it this way. I was struggling with some devastating family news, and this novel is about the only thing I read during the month of January 13 that took me out of grief, and absorbed me completely. I loved it.<br/><br/>More in a few months.<br/><br/>REREAD<br/><br/>It is said</span>
  <span id="freeText3588063412517282304" style="display:none">I read this novel in draft a year ago. I just checked to see when it would be published--April. So I will have more to say when I get the actual book.<br /><br />But it is on my buy-at-once list: since it's not out there is little to say that isn't spoilery. but put it this way. I was struggling with some devastating family news, and this novel is about the only thing I read during the month of January 13 that took me out of grief, and absorbed me completely. I loved it.<br /><br />More in a few months.<br /><br />REREAD<br /><br />It is said that Samuel Richardson, after being hectored by readers and critics following the runaway success of his novel <i>Clarissa (a success, one gathers from reading period chatter, due in large part to his witty villain Lovelace before his in</i>evitable and lugubrious end), promised he would write about a good man.<br /><br />So he gave the world Sir Charles Grandison, who was so firmly aware enough of his perfection that he converses lengthily to all and sundry between the busyness of kidnappings, abductions, defeating villains, etc. It’s interesting to me when reading reader reactions to these early novels that women seemed to enjoy Sir Charles more than men. Jane Austen, who had a very sharp eye for character in reality as well as in fiction, loved the novel so much she adapted it into a play.<br /><br />I’m going to come back to that as I try to feel my way through my reactions, but first: <i>The Goblin Emperor</i>’s Maia is, from the beginning, to the end, a good person. We the reader can see that—the first sign comes early on when, on being thrust summarily aboard an airship after discovering he is now the emperor of the elves, he takes the time to look into the faces of the crew. But he doesn’t see himself as good. He is aware of his shortcomings, and his inward struggle is as profound as the outward struggle against the many forces arrayed against him.<br /><br />At the start, the unwanted half-goblin fourth son is now emperor. <br /><br />Previous to this, Maia survived ten years of his cousin’s brutal guardianship, and before that, eight years of his gentle, spiritual mother’s loving influence. Maia is utterly unprepared for any life, really: the little he was allowed to learn was beaten into him by Setheris, who made certain Maia had an understanding of the exigencies of law, and of court.<br /><br />Maia’s first piece of luck is the probity of the courier who brought the news, Scevet <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One of my few, and mild, quibbles is that I would have liked to see a bit more development here. Scevet is almost too conveniently the dedicated guide, with no apparent life of his own.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Maia relies on Scevet to help him navigate the dangers of a court that actively as well as covertly does not want Maia as emperor.<br /><br />And so he must get himself crowned, get the dead buried, the cause of the accident investigated, and all the while deal with the inexorable press of responsibilities expected of an emperor.<b><br /><br />Kings</b><br /><br />I like stories about kings. Kings are, well, kings. Sometimes I get tired of democratic pearl-clutching about adolescent fantasy and its preoccupation with kings. Guess what, there are kings in all forms in all literature. Human beings don’t do anything without their hierarchies. I’m less interested in reading about cubicle bosses or alphas at high school or arrogant pundits on the literary scene than I am in stories in which the trappings are colorful, and grace and style are part of the equation. There’s a better chance of that kind of story with kings.<br /><br />But I lose interest fast if the kings don’t actually do any kinging. The weight of empire, the contradictions (the lack of privacy, and private time), the unending negotiation between balance and inertia, chaos and progress, those are some of the aspects I like about royal stories, and this one has got it right. Even the levels of language are not overlooked, or the several handwritings. These geeky details for the history buff give the world dimension.<b><br /><br />Worldbuilding</b><br /><br />This world is less magical than steam run. There are elves and goblins. The elves are Tolkien-pale, with beautiful hair and light eyes, but these are not Tolkien’s elves. They not only have pointed ears (stepping around the passionate sixties discussions of whether JRRT’s elves actually had pointed ears or not), but they are rather like dog or cat ears: they move, often reflecting emotions as well as responding to directional sound. <br /><br />These elves were not Tolkien’s elves, nor were they the emotionally adolescent prettyboy elves of many eighties fantasies. They aren’t “elfpunk.” There is almost no music in this elfland, no particular emphasis on the natural world: if anything, the elves in their complicated stone edifices hearken back to Tolkien’s dwarves. As far as I could tell there is little euphony in their words or names, long as they are: the long names with their syllabic and prefix patterns instead suggest a long and complicated history. The elves seem to live human spans of life, and of course can breed with other races.<br /><br />Their world evokes the late nineteenth century, undergoing technological and cultural change. Women in all the cultures seem to be bound to childbirth, at least at the upper levels of various societies. Wealth is based on the suffering of the poor working long hours in mines.<br /><br />Maia sees no problem with women realizing their desires outside of cultural mandated babymaker. I think I would have looked askance at that—seen it as preaching to the choir—except that Maia’s own emotional makeup, as powerless victim of abuse, is his motivation for empathetic action and compassion. “We were not seen as worth educating either,” that is perhaps the quintessential comment of the nineteenth century female gaze; it represents anyone marginalized, which was, in the west, basically everyone who wasn’t a white heterosexual landowning male. <br /><br />With reference to what I said above about Sir Charles, I think there could be an interesting wider discussion of male/female narrative gazes spinning off from this book, but I can see that this review is already long, so I think that that discussion will have to take place elsewhere.<br /><br />Suffice it to say that the book begins slowly, as the weight of responsibility threatens to crush Maia, who already knows what it is to be crushed: as he begins to push back, things happen. The gradual acceleration of the pace left me suddenly at the end. The story resolves, but oh, was I disappointed to discover that there isn’t more, just because I want to spend more time in that world, and with those people.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3588063412517282304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_882762840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882762840" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5238423-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352775557p2/5238423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/882762840?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/5238423-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=rated-4-star">rated-4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882762840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5682129686818559414"><a href='http://fantasyreviewbarn.com/fantasy-review-the-goblin-emperor-by-katherine-addison/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Review Barn</a><br/><br/>I finished The Goblin Emperor and found myself smiling. Not just from the joy of reading a really good book, but because for the first time in a long time I read a fantasy novel with a hopeful tone. Obviously the current trend of the genre is quite the opposite of hopeful, and those that break out of the dark tone tend to end with everything wrapped up in a package and happily ever after. But to end just on a hopeful tone? Well, that just causes smiles.<br/><br/>The blurb really tells y</span>
  <span id="freeText5682129686818559414" style="display:none"><a href="http://fantasyreviewbarn.com/fantasy-review-the-goblin-emperor-by-katherine-addison/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Review Barn</a><br /><br />I finished The Goblin Emperor and found myself smiling. Not just from the joy of reading a really good book, but because for the first time in a long time I read a fantasy novel with a hopeful tone. Obviously the current trend of the genre is quite the opposite of hopeful, and those that break out of the dark tone tend to end with everything wrapped up in a package and happily ever after. But to end just on a hopeful tone? Well, that just causes smiles.<br /><br />The blurb really tells you what you need to know. This tale opens with Maia being woken by his guardian to be given news of an airship crash that was carrying not only the emperor, but everyone ahead of Maia in the line of succession. Suddenly the half goblin, hated by his father and unknown to the court, must leave his exile to take the reign as Emperor. No longer subject to his guardians apathy and abuse, but all alone in the complex elven court, this is the story of a man over his head but doing what he can.<br /><br />I find myself struck by the realism of this book; specifically when it comes to character personalities and their interactions with each other. Maia is an outsider, an other, as unknown to the court as it is to him. Immediately he finds himself surrounded by false friends and those who feel they can hold power over him. In lesser hands the major players of the court would have come down to the good guys and the bad guys; many books promising political intrigue seem to fall into this trap. But Addison actually took the time to craft her characters; each has their own unique motivations. While those who are truly against Maia are hard to find common ground with, almost everyone else has motives that are believable and even sympathetic, even when the characters are putting a false face forward for Maia.<br /><br />As a main character Maia does not disappoint, a good thing because this is his story and his story alone. Though told in the third person the perspective never leaves his side. The hopeful tone I mentioned works because he is so likable. I felt his loneliness and isolation, understood his follies and false steps in court, and felt the joy for him as he discovered who in the court he could really count on, even hope to call a friend. He may be out of his depth but he is not naïve, and it led to interesting interactions.<br /><br />This is a book with long names and some strict speaking conventions that are unofficially enforced in court. As such I had a bit of a false start as I lost track of a couple of characters and had to back track and restart early in. But Addison was consistent in her use of the language, and most names had a shorted form, so it was not long before I was in the flow of the book and forgot I had any issues with it to begin with. It was a well-paced story, smart and interesting when a bit slower but with a bit more action than early reviews suggested sprinkled in. As an unlikely man on the throne and holder of some more liberal ideas he makes some real enemies, and they are not afraid to attempt some extreme measures. And while his dealings with the necessities of court makes up the main plot of the book, the question of his father’s death needs to be answered as well.<br /><br />My quibbles were minor; I really enjoyed almost every aspect of this book. I had a bit of an eye roll moment when a letter dealing with the investigation came in; handwritten and of much importance it was page after page of ‘this is what has been happening off the screen.’ And as big of a deal as his Goblin heritage seemed to be at first I was a bit surprised at how quickly certain parties were ok with it. Perhaps this is purely expectations; I expected this to be a bit more of a racial prejudice parallel that never really materialized. Or perhaps Addison was too successful, her subtlety messing with my expectations one more time.<br /><br />Almost every review I have read of this book thus far have pointed out that this book can be seen as the antithesis of the GRIMDARK trend. I can’t help but agree. With its slower but meaningful pace and hopeful tone I hope it gains a following that proves that this type of story has its place out there as well.<br /><br />4 Stars<br /><br />Review Copy received through NetGalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5682129686818559414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3097390995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3097390995" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/94602-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521304176p2/94602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3097390995?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/94602-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=grand-opera">grand-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=identity-crisis">identity-crisis</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=woundedsoulsandfragileflowers">woundedsoulsandfragileflowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=fantasy-and-scifi">fantasy-and-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=its-the-quiet-ones">its-the-quiet-ones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3097390995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4655214574047363178">This thing had a stick up its butt for the first 100 pages, removed it for about a hundred, and then poured a bag of saccharine all over itself and solemnly marched about to the tune of the Emperor’s New Clothes for the rest. After a hugely deceptive start with a charming intro of a language guide- yeah you heard me, super Strange & Norrell mischievous footnote vibes- it suddenly got Very Impressed with its own world building and took itself extremely seriously for way way too long. And while I </span>
  <span id="freeText4655214574047363178" style="display:none">This thing had a stick up its butt for the first 100 pages, removed it for about a hundred, and then poured a bag of saccharine all over itself and solemnly marched about to the tune of the Emperor’s New Clothes for the rest. After a hugely deceptive start with a charming intro of a language guide- yeah you heard me, super Strange &amp; Norrell mischievous footnote vibes- it suddenly got Very Impressed with its own world building and took itself extremely seriously for way way too long. And while I am as much of a linguistics nerd as I think anyone outside the field can probably stand to be, family names and a culture using the royal we does not a compelling narrative make. I excuse a lot from exposition sections in the same way I do tv pilots, but man this was tedious. Maia’s status as poor orphaned Oliver Twist did little to touch me because it was resolved too soon and never really made to feel real. The Elfin court is not mysterious and labyrinth as I was hoping, but full of boring meetings and and endless subplot about a bridge that won’t end. This author is a classic Won’t Kill My Darlings, but given that 21st century twist where she also won’t morally compromise main characters either. You are eeeevvvillllllll or good or delusional/crazy- those are your options here. After an actually successful joke by Maia woke me up almost exactly on pg 100 he kept it up with the relatable humanity for another hundred pages or so and then got swallowed up by world building again. The last part of this draaaaaggggggeeedddddd. Not least because all suspense was taken out of everything at all times. Good People Win Because Small Acts of Kindness Karma Be Nice Kids and No Worries Maia is Perfect. I just.... fine, but also I’m bored? One of my danger signs of a failing novel is if I’d rather leave the room and follow minor characters around than stay with the MC. Oh man so many in this book! Cala, #1. Kiru the lady mage who was made a big deal of and then disappeared. That Marquess dude and his BFF the snooty but nice House of Lords stand-ins- I’d watch that sitcom. So kudos for the secondary character ideas! But no one is there long enough for me to focus on- instead I keep winding up with Maia who keeps failing upwards or being blessed with magical statesmanlike instincts after a life of abused isolation and god knows he’ll pull it out of his ass every time and I’m so booorreeeddd. Guys, I majored in European history, I devour bowls of popcorn in front of all the courtly intrigue filled biographies there are, I have been an epic fantasy fan for two decades. This should so be my jam on so many levels and it is not. What is with the high ratings on this one? I held out on it for years to see if the star average would go down and it didn’t and so I ordered it and I don’t get it. What are you guys seeing that I’m missing?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4655214574047363178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1190781190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190781190" />
    <a title="Mona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7020601-mona"><img alt="Mona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392557851p2/7020601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1190781190?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mona" href="/user/show/7020601-mona">Mona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/23261150-the-goblin-emperor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1190781190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer937634168539470451"><b>Flawed but Likeable Coming-of-Age Fantasy Tale</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452181065i/17657418._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have mixed feelings about this novel.<br/><br/>I could have done with less of the unpronounceable and unspellable names and places (Edrahasivar, Varenechibel, the Untheileneise, etc.); elaborate rituals, and endless descriptions of dress and costume , as in the following passage:<br/><br/><i>"Maia suffered himself to be adorned. Rings for his fingers, silver set with jade and moonstones, bracelets like manacles, silver set with dull cabochon emeralds; a series of rings f</i></span>
  <span id="freeText937634168539470451" style="display:none"><b>Flawed but Likeable Coming-of-Age Fantasy Tale</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452181065i/17657418._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have mixed feelings about this novel.<br><br>I could have done with less of the unpronounceable and unspellable names and places (Edrahasivar, Varenechibel, the Untheileneise, etc.); elaborate rituals, and endless descriptions of dress and costume , as in the following passage:<br><br><i>"Maia suffered himself to be adorned. Rings for his fingers, silver set with jade and moonstones, bracelets like manacles, silver set with dull cabochon emeralds; a series of rings for his ears, more pale green jade; a necklace of moonstones and cabochon emeralds that clasped tight around his throat; a silver and moonstone diadem."</i><br><br>I think the story hides behind the endless arcane descriptions, impossible names, etc. These things don't really enhance the novel, but detract from it. They're fluff, not substance.<br><br>But I can't entirely dismiss the book. It's still moving and involving, because of its main character, Maia (a.k.a. Edrahasivar). At bottom, this is a coming of age story, based on the usual tropes. Abused and reviled child grows up and makes good. <br><br>Maia, a grey skinned elf/goblin hybrid, is exiled by his father, the cruel and capricious Emperor Varenechibel, because he (Maia's father) is forced into a political marriage with Maia's mother, Chenelo, a woman Maia's father doesn't love. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maia's mother, whom he adores, dies when he is eight. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Maia is raised in exile by his abusive cousin.<br><br>But then the entire royal family is killed in an airship accident and Maia's the only relative left alive. So, by default and to everyone's surprise, he becomes the Goblin Emperor, Edrahasivar the Seventh.<br><br>Maia/Edrahasivar's character is what drives the story. In contrast to the usual fantasy royalty, he isn't cruel, evil, ruthless, and self-serving. On the contrary, he is kind, compassionate, decent, and ethical. <br><br>He also confounds the expectations of others. Although his education has been spotty, he isn't stupid. In fact, he proves to be rather brilliant at statecraft. He builds bridges (literally and figuratively). He brings new ideas and viewpoints to the job of being Emperor.<br><br>He's not a pushover. People think he might be weak, because, as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe" title="Gene Wolfe" rel="nofollow noopener">Gene Wolfe</a><br>says, the world believes that "courtesy is weakness". Maia repeatedly demonstrates his ability to stand up to bullies and those who disrespect him.<br><br>The core of the story is Maia's evolution from a lonely, friendless and isolated boy to one who is held in love and affection by the people around him and has many friends. However, Addison does also emphasize the isolating nature of a high office such as Emperor.<br><br>His interactions with many people evolve (they have to, as an Emperor is never left alone). These include his future Empress, his bodyguards, various political allies and enemies, petitioners, his grandfather, etc.<br><br>There's something adolescent about this story idea. The special snowflake whose worth is finally recognized by the world. Life doesn't always work that way, kiddies.<br><br>Still, Maia's basic goodness and compassion are the core of the story. And he's not the least egotistical or vain. These qualities, along with his eye for innovative ideas, are what make him an excellent ruler.<br><br>The rest is just ornate ornamental fluff. <br><br>Kyle McCarley's audio reading was usually appropriate, although at times it seemed a bit pompous.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="937634168539470451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer886959680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17463225181666035089">Maia is the overlooked and unwanted half-goblin son of the Emperor of the Elves. Then his father and older brothers die in a dirigible explosion. In the space of a single day, Maia is catapulted from a shabby genteel life in the backwater to head of an Imperial Court he has only ever visited once before. Maia tries to be a good emperor, but his upbringing didn't prepare him for any part of his new life.<br/><br/>I really, really liked this, both the world that Addison has created and Maia himself. I only </span>
  <span id="freeText17463225181666035089" style="display:none">Maia is the overlooked and unwanted half-goblin son of the Emperor of the Elves. Then his father and older brothers die in a dirigible explosion. In the space of a single day, Maia is catapulted from a shabby genteel life in the backwater to head of an Imperial Court he has only ever visited once before. Maia tries to be a good emperor, but his upbringing didn't prepare him for any part of his new life.<br /><br />I really, really liked this, both the world that Addison has created and Maia himself. I only wish the story had been a little less episodic, and the conspiracies a little harder to uncover. But that aside, I cannot wait to read more of this series!<br /><br />ETA on 3/15/18 I keep rereading this book. It's become one of my favorite comfort reads, up there with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2156.Persuasion" title="Persuasion by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener"> Persuasion</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3008.A_Little_Princess" title="A Little Princess by Frances Hodgson Burnett" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Little Princess</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345560.The_Making_of_a_Marchioness" title="The Making of a Marchioness by Frances Hodgson Burnett" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Making of a Marchioness</a>. I guess I love solidly decent, sensitive characters in very well described settings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17463225181666035089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211382657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1752853051306485554">I probably would not have read this book if it hadn't been selected for the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sword and Laser</a> book club for March 2015, and in the same month get announced as one of the Nebula nominees. <br/><br/>It's not my normal fare, in other words. It was described to me as a steampunk-fantasy court drama novel, but I would characterize it more as a coming of age, fish out of water, court drama novel. The steampunk is far in the background and as much as I don't geek out about those kinds of details, I think more of t</span>
  <span id="freeText1752853051306485554" style="display:none">I probably would not have read this book if it hadn't been selected for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword and Laser</a> book club for March 2015, and in the same month get announced as one of the Nebula nominees. <br /><br />It's not my normal fare, in other words. It was described to me as a steampunk-fantasy court drama novel, but I would characterize it more as a coming of age, fish out of water, court drama novel. The steampunk is far in the background and as much as I don't geek out about those kinds of details, I think more of them would have made the world more interesting - more magic too, please! It's there, but so far in the background.<br /><br />The other parts of the world, from the elaborate family names to the complex kingdom rulership borders, to the elfin-goblin conflicts, were interesting and didn't feel like many other things. Actually I did keep thinking of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6437061.The_Hundred_Thousand_Kingdoms__The_Inheritance_Trilogy___1_" title="The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms (The Inheritance Trilogy, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hundred Thousand Kingdoms</a> by N.K. Jemisin but I'm not sure others will see the parallels.<br /><br />The best part, in my opinion, is the character of Maia the goblin emperor. I think the author writes him very compassionately, although flawed. He has quite the wardrobe.<br /><br />I am surprised this isn't the first in a trilogy or series because it feels like everything just gets settled by the end, and after all of this world has been created, it might be nice for the author to keep writing in it. <br /><br />You would think this fulfilled my fantasy reading for the year, but no. My usually post-modern literary book club has selected a fantasy novel for our next read, one I never would have read.... well here we go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1752853051306485554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_854181540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/854181540" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/854181540?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer854181540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11682496812825509550">A perfect court intrigue.<br/><br/>Maia never expected to become much of anyone. Although he’s technically a prince, after his mother died his father the emperor relegated him to exile at a remote manor, under the care of an abusive guardian. He never really expected to escape his position of disfavor, due to his mixed racial heritage. However, when a terrible airship accident not only kills his father, but also wipes out all the other people ahead of him in line for the succession, in one fell blow, Maia</span>
  <span id="freeText11682496812825509550" style="display:none">A perfect court intrigue.<br /><br />Maia never expected to become much of anyone. Although he’s technically a prince, after his mother died his father the emperor relegated him to exile at a remote manor, under the care of an abusive guardian. He never really expected to escape his position of disfavor, due to his mixed racial heritage. However, when a terrible airship accident not only kills his father, but also wipes out all the other people ahead of him in line for the succession, in one fell blow, Maia is unexpectedly recalled to court to take up the crown.<br /><br />Although unprepared for this responsibility, he’s determined to make a go of it, and give it his best shot. However, the swirl of sophisticated society is overwhelming to him, let alone the nuances of ruling an empire. And although Maia would like to make friends, enemies are already waiting for him.<br /><br />I requested this book without reading up on anything about it. At 16% of the way through, I said, ‘no way this is a debut author – the writing is too sharply honed,’ and I looked it up. It’s Sarah Monette! I LOVE Sarah Monette! (And I believe I actually read about this book coming out under a pseudonym on her blog, several years ago, but forgot about it!)<br /><br />No matter what name she uses, this is a truly excellent work. The characters are finely drawn, and treated with sensitivity. There’s a constant, well-paced tension as Maia navigates this new and alien world, forms alliances, discovers plots, and tries to investigate his father’s death. The concerns of different factions of the aristocracy, the working classes, women, and different cultures are all dealt with for a complex, convincing setting. The positioning of elves and goblins at the brink of an Industrial Revolution(?) is unusual but convincingly done, without any sacrifice of ‘magic’ and the rich panoply of a faerie court. Even the language and the social hierarchy felt fresh and new.<br /><br />I know it’s only February, but I wouldn’t be at all surprised if this is the best book I’ll read this year.<br /><br />I received an advance copy of this book from NetGalley. Thanks to NetGalley and Tor/Forge.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11682496812825509550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1504231732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1504231732" />
    <a title="Doug" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33038913-doug"><img alt="Doug" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515035780p2/33038913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1504231732?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug" href="/user/show/33038913-doug">Doug</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1504231732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9593197888354310346">A book whose quality totally caught me off-guard, and one of the best books I've read all year.<br/><br/>I was dragging my feet when it came to reading this book because the title made it seem to me like it was going to be much zanier than it was. In fact, this book is one of the few fantasy books I've read that treats its reader like they are intelligent. Sure, the Malazan series takes its reader to be intelligent too, but it's in a very different way: the Malazan books leave a lot implicit and subtextua</span>
  <span id="freeText9593197888354310346" style="display:none">A book whose quality totally caught me off-guard, and one of the best books I've read all year.<br /><br />I was dragging my feet when it came to reading this book because the title made it seem to me like it was going to be much zanier than it was. In fact, this book is one of the few fantasy books I've read that treats its reader like they are intelligent. Sure, the Malazan series takes its reader to be intelligent too, but it's in a very different way: the Malazan books leave a lot implicit and subtextual; not everything is on the page. This book, on the other hand, lets each event and episode be pretty much easily understood, but hits you over the head with names, people, etc., so much that you feel completely immersed. This book pulls no punches when it comes to giving you a world, even if it (very often) comes at the expense of your memory.<br /><br />This book is not at all action-y. In a sense, it is all politics. It's about a young adult who becomes emperor unexpectedly: nobody really knows who he is, and he has no idea what he's doing. He's well-meaning but entirely in over his head.<br /><br />But this is not a book about political intrigue, even though it sometimes comes across that way. It's a book about coping: coping with your life, with who you are, and who you have to be. It's a book about loss and commemoration, and about redemption. It's the fantasy genre at its very best. And it doesn't try to shoehorn in any action or military scenes/plots. This book focuses squarely on emotional development dressed up as political intrigue.<br /><br />It's also a deeply heartfelt book with a warmth that I would not have anticipated from a story about a goblin becoming emperor.<br /><br />It's one of my favourite fantasy books, and perhaps the best book I read all year, but it's not perfect. The main character is a little too "good," too much of an angel, too "sensitive," especially against the backdrop of a culture that isn't at all that way, and I find that a cheap way of selling the character to the reader. It also struck me as a bit one-dimensional. This character feels lots of things in response to his circumstances, but his anger and hatred never really boil over, and he's always too "good" even when it comes to moderating that anger.<br /><br />But this book is fantastic and really worth the read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9593197888354310346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
